[2026-02-07T16:22:21Z] Akshay: It’s a speed reading assist and to help with focus, it’s a font called bionic reading. ↵ https://bionic-reading.com/
[2026-02-07T16:22:38Z] Akshay: The efficacy of this is highly debated btw, but it works really well for me
[2026-02-07T16:22:55Z] Abhishek S: Oh wow, hadn't even noticed it
[2026-02-07T16:23:33Z] Akshay: The idea is it makes your eyes focus on the bolded initial part of the word and lets your brain complete the rest, saving u the time of reading it
[2026-02-07T16:23:52Z] Akshay: Again, experts think its a scam but honestly it has worked amazingly well for me so
[2026-02-07T16:27:01Z] Akshay: Readwise did a study on whether it works. ↵ You can try it here if you want to check if it works for you. ↵ https://blog.readwise.io/does-bionic-reading-actually-work/
[2026-02-07T16:29:16Z] Akshay: For me comprehension didnt really improve but it was easily minimum 5% faster. When you have to read a lot, it adds up. IME. ‎<This message was edited>

[2026-02-07T19:01:10Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Hawaaizaada was inspired by the biography of Shivkar Bapuji Talpade, a resident of Bombay, is claimed to have constructed and flown an unmanned, heavier-than-air aircraft in 1895. Contemporary accounts of a successful flight do not exist, and no reliable historical records document its existence. Pseudo-historical narratives about Talpade proliferated in India in the early 2000s among adherents of the Hindu-nationalist right-wing. These included the false claim that Talpade had "invented the modern aircraft". ↵ The 2015 Indian Science Congress ancient aircraft controversy refers to protests that occurred during the 102nd Indian Science Congress in Mumbai on 4 January 2015 when a paper claiming to prove that aircraft were invented in the Vedic age was allowed to be presented.

[2026-02-07T19:02:54Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Some versions of the story say that Talpade had advice from Subbaraya Shastry (1866 - 1940), who later wrote Vaimānika Shāstra ("Science of Aeronautics"), a text that is frequently associated with descriptions of aircraft in the Vedas. A 1974 paper by scientists from the Indian Institute of Science declared that the designs in the Vaimānika Shāstra itself were technologically unfeasible, stating that the text showed a "complete lack of understanding of the dynamics of the flight of heavier-than-air craft".

[2026-02-08T16:47:20Z] Ryan Colaço: Q. ↵ 6. The name we use today is a bit of a geographical accident. An Italian mapmaker and geographer named Alvise Cadamosto, translated the name into his own language as who was working with the Portuguese. Because his maps were so widely distributed throughout Europe, the lItalian version stuck, and the British eventually kept it and spread it. The most popular theory for the original name *is* that the shape of the mountains trappd moisture and caused frequent, violent, thunderstorms. The echo of the thunder rolling through the peaks sounded to the sailors like the roar of a lion.
